<div id="review_1760193938" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1760193938" />
    <a title="Lance Shadow" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/46445602-lance-shadow"><img alt="Lance Shadow" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1474240407p2/46445602.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1760193938?book_show_action=true">Aug 08, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lance Shadow" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lance Shadow" href="/user/show/46445602-lance-shadow">Lance Shadow</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/46445602-lance-shadow?shelf=darth-bane-trilogy">darth-bane-trilogy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/46445602-lance-shadow?shelf=legends">legends</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/46445602-lance-shadow?shelf=novels">novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/46445602-lance-shadow?shelf=star-wars">star-wars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1760193938" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17967254120140159304">Well, this is a journey I should have embarked on long ago, but I have finally made it to the end. With it's final chapter complete, I have at last reached the milestone of reading (and reviewing) <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16071610.The_Darth_Bane_Series__Star_Wars_Darth_Bane__1_3_' title='The Darth Bane Series (Star Wars Darth Bane #1-3) by Drew Karpyshyn' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Darth Bane Series</a>!<br/><br/>Before I get to this one, I'll recap my thoughts on the previous books in this series. <br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/35430.Path_of_Destruction__Star_Wars_Darth_Bane___1_' title='Path of Destruction (Star Wars Darth Bane, #1) by Drew Karpyshyn' rel='nofollow noopener'>Path of Destruction</a> is good, but I think it is an overrated book. It has great action sequences and does a good job with Darth Bane's origin story and how he created the rule of two, but there i</span>
  <span id="freeText17967254120140159304" style="display:none">Well, this is a journey I should have embarked on long ago, but I have finally made it to the end. With it's final chapter complete, I have at last reached the milestone of reading (and reviewing) <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16071610.The_Darth_Bane_Series__Star_Wars_Darth_Bane__1_3_" title="The Darth Bane Series (Star Wars Darth Bane #1-3) by Drew Karpyshyn" rel="nofollow noopener">The Darth Bane Series</a>!<br /><br />Before I get to this one, I'll recap my thoughts on the previous books in this series. <br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/35430.Path_of_Destruction__Star_Wars_Darth_Bane___1_" title="Path of Destruction (Star Wars Darth Bane, #1) by Drew Karpyshyn" rel="nofollow noopener">Path of Destruction</a> is good, but I think it is an overrated book. It has great action sequences and does a good job with Darth Bane's origin story and how he created the rule of two, but there is a large amount of page time devoted to boring secondary characters who no only don't add anything to Bane's character, their subplots actively detract from the story, and make Bane's efforts to create the Rule of Two look foolish. In the end, I liked it, even if I don't consider it to be the masterpiece it's hyped up to be. <br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1347837.Rule_of_Two__Star_Wars_Darth_Bane___2_" title="Rule of Two (Star Wars Darth Bane, #2) by Drew Karpyshyn" rel="nofollow noopener">Rule of Two</a> was a significant improvement over Path of Destruction for me. Bane's orbalisk armor may have been dumb, but I loved everything else about the book: the story had a well-constructed action thriller setup, the characters on both sides of the conflict were interesting, and I thought Karpyshyn did a great job transitioning the Old Republic era of the Star Wars timeline into that of the pre-<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34941.The_Phantom_Menace__Star_Wars_Novelizations___1_" title="The Phantom Menace (Star Wars Novelizations, #1) by Terry Brooks" rel="nofollow noopener">Phantom Menace</a> era, using it to add some very high stakes to the story he was telling in this book. Overall, Rule of Two was a very solid novel. <br /><br />Now we get to Dynasty of Evil. I didn't hate it, but this was quite easily my least favorite of the three. <br /><br />THE STORY: Ten years have passed since Darth Bane and his apprentice, Darth Zannah, evaded near-destruction from the jedi order. Now believed to be extinct, the Sith have been able to operate in the shadows. But Darth Bane has lost faith in Zannah, who has yet to challenge him for his title of Master of the Sith. He needs to find a new apprentice, but the use of the dark side has taken a toll on his body. Hence, he searches for the holocron of an ancient Sith Lord, as well as a new apprentice- even though Zannah is, in fact, preparing to take him down. <br /><br />THE BAD: Despite having the fewest actual flaws out of the trilogy, I wasn't all that impressed with this book. It doesn't do anything to much that is actively wrong- it doesn't ruin the established characters, nothing happens that egregiously breaks Star Wars lore, and there's no moment that made me roll my eyes. <br /><br />No, the biggest issue I have with this book is that I didn't understand what the point was. The book is barely over 300 pages long, and feels like it struggled to get there. I got the sense that the only part of this book Drew Karpyshyn was interested in was the final battle between Bane and Zannah, but Del Rey wanted to make this story a trilogy because that was the tradition for the majority of storylines at the time. As a result, what probably should have been told as a comic book miniseries at best is stretched out with a series of anemic subplots thinly woven together so they could stretch themselves into feature-novel length, with even the final confrontation being stretched into two segments. <br />In the end, I just didn't see the point. The second book finished on such a strong note. Bane and Zannah had such an amazing dynamic, only to have it be yanked away with a hasty exposition dump at the very start of the book. Because of this, I found the opening of this book very jarring and it took me some time to get used to the story being told. And looking back, I would have been better off filling things in with my imagination. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ at the end of Book 2, Zannah tells Bane she will kill him eventually, but she still had more to learn. with that, I could have just filled in the blanks instead of be disappointed when Bane and Zannah barely interact in Book 3  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. <br />On top of that, I was ultimately underwhelmed by the character of Serra. Her purpose in the story is pretty small for how much page time is devoted to her point of view- and it feels like she only has so much time devoted to her because she is connected to the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/390081.Jedi_vs__Sith" title="Jedi vs. Sith by Darko Macan" rel="nofollow noopener">Jedi vs. Sith</a> comic. Karpyshyn either gave Serra such a big portion of this book because he is is obviously a big fan of Jedi vs. Sith, or it was out of obligation because the other two books in this trilogy heavily feature characters from Jedi vs. Sith (Path of Destruction has Kaan/Kopecz/Githany/Hoth/Farfalla, while Rule of Two has Darovit). What was ultimately disappointing about her character was that she started off with an interesting concept, only for Karpyshyn to not commit, go the safe route, and try to make her likeable and sympathetic in the last third. Unfortunately, I just didn't buy her change of heart in the end. <br /><br />Lastly, the book bills itself as "A Novel of the Old Republic" but it really doesn't feel like an old republic era book. It feels more like a pre-phantom menace era one; and there's a big difference. Path of Destruction is 100% an Old Republic novel. A large portion of Rule of Two took place in 990 BBY, after the Old Republic era had officially ended. But that book did a great job making itself feel like an Old Republic era novel all the way through- it struck the perfect balance between Old Republic and Pre-Phantom Menace, allowing it to work as the perfect transitional piece for Star Wars Lore. Dynasty of Evil feels completely like a pre-Phantom Menace era book. At best, it's an "epilogue" to the Old Republic but even then I believe that's a stretch because nothing in the worldbuilding connects to the Old Republic. Sure it focuses on characters who have been alive since the Old Republic era, but the state of the galaxy feels exactly the same as it does during <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11099729.Darth_Plagueis" title="Darth Plagueis by James Luceno" rel="nofollow noopener">Darth Plagueis</a> and of course The Phantom Menace. <br /><br />THE GOOD: Despite the lack of necessity that I had while reading this book, there is enough that is well-executed for me to have been happy I gave this book a try. <br />Despite undertaking in boring storylines, the characters themselves were fairly interesting. I was invested in the characters themselves, even if I didn't care about what they were doing. <br />Bane and Zannah don't have much added to them that I couldn't get out of the previous books, but they were interesting enough. They still had a good amount of personality, and were exciting to read about when they were in the middle of an action sequence. <br />Aside from Serra, I enjoyed the secondary characters. "The Huntress" was really cool. And Set Harth was actually pretty fun with some decent humor. He added a sense of levity to a series which has been focused on being dark and gritty to the point where it sometimes became edgy- but the levity Harth offered never felt out of place. On top of that, Karpyshyn does a good job integrating their stories into that of Bane and Zannah, even if again, none of the storylines whether primary or secondary were all that interesting. <br /><br />What salvaged this book at all for me was the final confrontation between Bane and Zannah, which is legitimately worth getting too. Stretching the fight scene out to two stages may have been a desperate way to stretch out the page count, but I ended up not caring. Both stages of the fight were exciting, intense, and well choreographed. And the ending to the fight was AWESOME. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Drew Karpyshyn took to his blog to set the record straight that Zannah indeed ultimately wins, but I love how ambiguous he wrote it in the book- Did Zannah succeed in killing Bane and taking up the mantle of Sith master, or did Bane succeed in taking over Zannah's body through essence transfer?  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />And until then, there's several good action scenes earlier in the book. And this is the one aspect of the book that is done better in Dynasty of Evil than in Rule of Two- the fights involving Bane were filled with tension. Who knew that by taking away the Orbalisk armor, I would be worried about what happened to Bane, and hence be invested in the fight scenes?<br /><br />THE CONCLUSION: Final rating is 3.5 stars, rounded down because I can't find a reason why this had to be a feature-length novel. <br />This book clearly is meant for one thing: the final showdown between Darth Bane and Darth Zannah for who ultimately will become the undisputed master of the dark side. And if that's all you care about in this book, it delivers. <br />While it has enough good action and good characterization that I am glad to have read it, I think this story would have worked better as a comic book miniseries. Then we could have seen this fight sequence play out in a visual format, and I wouldn't have had to trudge through a meh novel that struggled to justify its own existence. <br />As is, I feel like this book only exists to give this series that "trilogy" categorization that is so popular with star wars books. It should have stayed as a duology- with the first one showing the rise of Darth Bane and the subsequent fall of the sith and its reformation into the Rule of Two. The second one would be about how the Rule of Two establishes itself and survives through a parallel reformation of the Republic. Unfortunately, while it does not actively ruin anything by existing, this third book adds nothing to the Old Republic era and very little to the story of Darth Bane that I couldn't have gotten from its predecessors. <br /><br />If you just want to see what happens to Bane and Zannah, Dynasty of Evil will most likely be satisfactory. Otherwise, the best I can say about it is that it's fine. I don't hate this book, but it's my least favorite in the series.<br /><br />The Darth Bane Trilogy is a series that I found enjoyable, but does not live up to the reputation that it gets among Star Wars fans. All of these books have some great, even fantastic things in them, but they also have serious problems. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1347837.Rule_of_Two__Star_Wars_Darth_Bane___2_" title="Rule of Two (Star Wars Darth Bane, #2) by Drew Karpyshyn" rel="nofollow noopener">Rule of Two</a> was easily my favorite of the three, and the one that most closely resembles what I thought I would get after all the hype that surrounds the Darth Bane Trilogy. Compared to Drew Karpyshyn's other, more recent star wars work, its mixed. All three books in the Bane trilogy are better than <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10687840.Revan__Star_Wars_The_Old_Republic___1_" title="Revan (Star Wars The Old Republic, #1) by Drew Karpyshyn" rel="nofollow noopener">Revan</a>, but the only one that could hope to reach the heights of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13533656.Annihilation__Star_Wars_The_Old_Republic___4_" title="Annihilation (Star Wars The Old Republic, #4) by Drew Karpyshyn" rel="nofollow noopener">Annihilation</a> is the second book. In terms of Old Republic era stories, I think they're the most overrated hands down. Rule of Two might make my top 5, but the others would not even come close. In conclusion, I think the Darth Bane trilogy is worth reading either for a repeat experience or for the first time. However, for me personally I've read better.</span>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('grYWVQZPPShhLrJTJfPYKJf0TB9xpvfMv01FY5LR9ie3OJnRnN+z0tPbandZiQ+ZvinioOOEbNHMwOpD3hA0cw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

And, to some extent, that was true. Anakin was dead. From the site of Anakin Skywalker s last stand on the molten surface of the planet Mustafar, where he sought to destroy his friend and former master, Obi-Wan Kenobi a fearsome specter in black has risen. Once the most powerful Knight ever known to the Jedi Order, he is now a disciple of the dark side, a lord of the dreaded Sith, and the avenging right hand of the galaxy s ruthless new Emperor. Seduced, deranged, and destroyed by the machinations of the Dark Lord Sidious, Anakin Skywalker is dead . . . and Darth Vader lives. Word of the events that created him the Jedi Council s failed mutiny against Supreme Chancellor Palpatine, the self-crowned Emperor s retaliatory command to exterminate the Jedi Order, and Anakin s massacre of his comrades and Masters in the Jedi Temple has yet to reach all quarters. When the three narrowly elude execution and become the desperate prey in a hunt across space it s neither clone soldiers, nor the newly deployed stormtroopers, nor even the wrath of the power-hungry Emperor himself they must fear most. The deadliest threat rests in the hideously swift and lethal crimson lightsaber of Darth Vader behind whose brooding mask lies a shattered heart, a poisoned soul, and a cunning, twisted mind hell-bent on vengeance. For the handful of scattered Jedi, survival is imperative if the light side of the Force is to be protected and the galaxy somehow, someday reclaimed. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer7861573091157229566">Drew Karpyshyn is a Canadian author and game designer. After working at a credit union for some time, he eventually became a game developer. He joined BioWare towards the end of the Baldur's Gate series, and wrote the tie-in novel for Baldur's Gate II: Throne of Bhaal. He stayed with BioWare, where he worked on Neverwinter Nights, and became the Senior Writer on the critically acclaimed Star Wars:</span>
  <span id="freeText7861573091157229566" style="display:none">Drew Karpyshyn is a Canadian author and game designer. After working at a credit union for some time, he eventually became a game developer. He joined BioWare towards the end of the Baldur's Gate series, and wrote the tie-in novel for Baldur's Gate II: Throne of Bhaal. He stayed with BioWare, where he worked on Neverwinter Nights, and became the Senior Writer on the critically acclaimed Star Wars: Knights of the Old Republic.<br /><br />This Star Wars connection gave him the opportunity to write <u>Darth Bane: Path of Destruction</u>, his first hardcover. Karpyshyn still works for BioWare where he is the lead writer for the Mass Effect series.</span>
